  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f5fcadef-0129-4204-8641-d519c52b9853'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer6012011055309009932">In a society steeped in tradition, Princess Lia’s life follows a preordained course. As First Daughter, she is expected to have the revered gift of sight—but she doesn’t—and she knows her parents are perpetrating a sham when they arrange her marriage to secure an alliance with a neighboring kingdom—to a prince she has never met.<br/><br/>On the morning of her wedding, Lia flees to a</span>
  <span id="freeText6012011055309009932" style="display:none">In a society steeped in tradition, Princess Lia’s life follows a preordained course. As First Daughter, she is expected to have the revered gift of sight—but she doesn’t—and she knows her parents are perpetrating a sham when they arrange her marriage to secure an alliance with a neighboring kingdom—to a prince she has never met.<br /><br />On the morning of her wedding, Lia flees to a distant village. She settles into a new life, hopeful when two mysterious and handsome strangers arrive—and unaware that one is the jilted prince and the other an assassin sent to kill her. Deception abounds, and Lia finds herself on the brink of unlocking perilous secrets—even as she finds herself falling in love. <br /><i><br />The Kiss of Deception </i>is the first audiobook in Mary E. Pearson's Remnant Chronicles</span>
  <a data-text-id="6012011055309009932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<div id="review_827878085" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/827878085" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/827878085?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer827878085" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12936166701863474345">I present you a short version of the book: <b>
  <i>Kiss of Deception: A Greek Dramedy</i>
</b>. A Dramedy, not to be confused with a dromedary, because a dromedary only has one hump. This story has two humps. THAT'S RIGHT, LADIES AND GENTLEMEN, WE HAVE <b>A FUCKING LOVE TRIANGLE</b>.<br/><br/>The entire play can be set on one stage with almost no scenery changes because I swear to fucking god nothing fucking happens in this book. It is not a high fantasy when the main character spends the entire fucking half of the book pret</span>
  <span id="freeText12936166701863474345" style="display:none">I present you a short version of the book: <b>
  <i>Kiss of Deception: A Greek Dramedy</i>
</b>. A Dramedy, not to be confused with a dromedary, because a dromedary only has one hump. This story has two humps. THAT'S RIGHT, LADIES AND GENTLEMEN, WE HAVE <b>A FUCKING LOVE TRIANGLE</b>.<br><br>The entire play can be set on one stage with almost no scenery changes because I swear to fucking god nothing fucking happens in this book. It is not a high fantasy when the main character spends the entire fucking half of the book pretending to be a serving maid, daydreaming, and trying to decide which of two mysterious strangers she likes more.<br><br><b>Every Greek play has a Chorus. Here, the Chorus is me, Khanh.</b> Wearing a blanket over my head because I don't have a white bathrobe. Also, I'm at work, and even in my cubicle, they'd probably frown upon me wearing a bathrobe, however chill my boss is.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409179428i/10944887.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Khanh: Greek Chorus. Close enough.<br><br>The Characters:<br><br><u>
  <b>Lia</b>
</u>: a lovely young 17-year old <b>Princess</b> of a generic High Fantasy Kingdom<br><br><u>
  <b>Pauline</b>
</u>: her devoted <b>maidservant</b> who is devoted to devoting her job and devoting her life to her princess<br><br><u>
  <b>The Assassin</b>
</u>: the fucking moron sent to kill Lia, who can't do his fucking job!<br><br><u>
  <b>The Prince</b>
</u>: the prince who got jilted by Lia when she runs away, he pursues her only to fall further in love with her!<br><br><u>Act I</u>:<br>Lia: I am a princess! I am rebellious! I am worthless! It is my wedding day and I'm going to run away because I can't bear to be trapped in a marriage that will secure the peace between the two nations and I think my future husband is going to be a hideous old douchebag!<br><br>Pauline: You're right, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: He probably smells, too!!! But what about the peace?!<br><br>Lia: Let's run away after completely ruining a centuries-old gown and completely disregarding all tradition! Screw my family! Screw them, I say!<br><br>Pauline: Whatever you say, my lady! I will abandon my position, risk my life, abandon my long-time love, Mikael, leave everything I have ever known behind in order to fulfill your wish!<br><br>Chorus: That's a bit much, don't you think?<br><br>Lia and Pauline: Nay! We're running away right now! *hops on horses and rides off*<br><br>Chorus: This is a high fantasy!<br><br><u>Act II</u>:<br>The Assassin: I am an assassin! I will find Princess Lia! I will kill her, because it's my motherfucking job!<br><br>The Prince: I am a prince! The prince who was supposed to marry Lia. I am neither old, decrepit, or smelly! I will only chase after Lia because I have to. Falling in love is totally out of the question.<br><br>Chorus: But do you smell?<br><br>The Prince: No!<br><br>The Assassin: Oh, hi, random stranger, fancy meeting you here.<br><br>The Prince: Oh, yo, man. What are you doing in these neck of the woods?<br><br>The Assassin: Just chilling, man, you know. Wanna travel together?<br><br>The Prince: Sure, let's find an inn in a small town and be roomies.<br><br>Chorus: ARE YOU FUCKING KIDDING ME?! HOW THE FUCK DID YOU GUYS FIND EACH OTHER WITHIN 2 CHAPTERS?<br><br>The Prince and the Assassin: Shut up.<br><br><u>Act III:</u><br>Lia: We've arrived! There are barbarians on the road, and we are two sheltered young woman who have never ventured outside of the palace before, but somehow we've magically made it there safely, eluding everyone pursuing us and leaving no clues as to where we've gone!<br><br>Pauline: Yes, my lady! You're so smart, my lady! You're so brave, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: How the fuck?!<br><br>Lia: Now we are going to settle ourselves down in a small seaside town, and I will pretend to be a waitress, never having waited on anyone in my entire life.<br><br>Pauline: Whatever you say, my lady.<br><br>Lia: I'm going to be a waitress at an inn like I've been doing it my whole life!<br><br>Pauline: You shit roses, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: THIS IS A HIGH FANTASY!<br><br>Lia: But hark, what are these two handsome young gentleman over there, a "fisherman" and a "farmer?!" Such handsome young men. So sleek! So refined! It's like they're not who they claim to be at all!<br><br>The Assassin: *steps aside for a monologue* I can't kill her. One glimpse at her and she has stolen my soul, and I'm not even 10% into the book yet ;_;<br><br>Chorus: DUDE, YOU'VE KNOWN HER FOR 5 SECONDS.<br><br>The Prince: *steps aside for a monologue* She is lovely! Such spirit! I have never seen the likes of it! Whoever thought she could be <b>so special, so different</b>! This is the girl I had hoped never to marry?! I'm in love! I'm driven mad with hunger!<br><br>Chorus: DUDE, YOU'VE KNOWN HER FOR 5 SECONDS.<br><br>The Assassin and the Prince: *together* Sup, guuuuuuuuuurl!<br><br>Chorus: GUYS, THIS IS A HIGH FANTASY!!!!!!!!!<br><br><u>Act IV</u>:<br>Lia: I'm a waitress! *giggles*<br><br>Pauline: You poop rainbows, my lady!<br><br>Lia: Look at me, waitressing! *laughs*<br><br>Pauline: I will lick your feet, my lady!<br><br>Lia: Look at me, pouring all these beers!<br><br>Pauline: So brilliantly poured, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: Can't you do something else? THIS IS A HIGH FANTASY<br><br>Pauline: Shut up! Don't listen to her, my lady!<br><br>Lia: Look at me!!!!!! I'm carrying plates to people's tables! *smiles widely*<br><br>Chorus: SERIOUSLY, IT'S BEEN ALMOST HALF THE FUCKING BOOK. DO SOMETHING.<br><br>Lia: I am! I'm a waitress in a small seaside town!<br><br>Pauline: I'll wear your used menstrual pads as shoes, my lady!<br><br>The Assassin: Lia, you're an uptight bitch!<br><br>Lia: *swoons*<br><br>The Prince: *smiles gently at Lia from afar*<br><br>Lia: Let's pick berries together!<br><br>Chorus: YOU'RE SERIOUSLY PICKING BERRIES IN THE FOREST?! THIS IS A HIGH FANTASY!<br><br>Lia: That's not all I'm doing! I'm not just picking berries...I'm....<br><br>Lia &amp; Chorus: A WAITRESS<br><br>Chorus: OK, I GET IT. BERRIES. BERRIES!!!!!<br><br>Pauline: You're doing great, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: THIS IS A HIGH FANTASY?!<br><br><u>Act V:</u><br><br>Lia: I'm a waitress! Look at me waiter! Wait, is that the right word? *laughs*<br><br>The Prince: You're so charming, Lia!<br><br>The Assassin: Wait a minute, I'm an assassin! I'm going to assassinate her! And by that, I mean I'm going to slowly fall in love with her!<br><br>Chorus: YOU'RE AN ASSASSIN!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1409191487i/10946457.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lia: Watch me! I'm a waitress! It's so hard! *laughs*<br><br>Pauline: You're doing wonderfully, my lady!<br><br>Lia: I'm a waitress! Look at me!<br><br>Pauline: You're a natural, my lady!<br><br>Lia: I'm a waitress! Look at me wash dishes!<br><br>Pauline: Fantastic, my lady!<br><br>Chorus: I FUCKING GIVE UP<br><br>Lia: Wait, already? But...but you don't even know what happens to me!!!!!!!! Between now and the end of the book, I'm probably going to sprout magical powers out of nowhere, fall in love, and then save a country, ALL WHILE BEING A WAITRESS IN A SEASIDE TOWN. Don't you want to stick around and find out?<br><br>Chorus: NO. *PUNCHES LIA IN THE FACE*<br><br>The end. Because I say so.<br><br>DNF at 50%, in case I didn't make that very clear.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_847563433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/847563433" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/847563433?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805099232" href="/book/show/18490681-the-kiss-of-deception">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847563433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12946406383725803358"><blockquote>
  <i>“Is he the first boy you ever kissed?” I asked<br/>“Who says I’ve kissed him?” Pauline replied mischievously. We both laughed. Girls of the royal staff were not supposed to indulge in such unrestrained behaviours.<br/>“Well, if you were to kiss him, what do you think it would be like?”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I have a question - <b>who cares?</b><br/><br/>Ugh, this book. I rarely give much weight to fantasy titles. They're almost always called "dramatic word of dramatic word" or "dramatic word and dramatic word", but I realize in hindsight th</span>
  <span id="freeText12946406383725803358" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Is he the first boy you ever kissed?” I asked<br />“Who says I’ve kissed him?” Pauline replied mischievously. We both laughed. Girls of the royal staff were not supposed to indulge in such unrestrained behaviours.<br />“Well, if you were to kiss him, what do you think it would be like?”</i>
</blockquote><br />I have a question - <b>who cares?</b><br /><br />Ugh, this book. I rarely give much weight to fantasy titles. They're almost always called "dramatic word of dramatic word" or "dramatic word and dramatic word", but I realize in hindsight that I should have paid attention to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_" title="The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Deception</a> because, I kid you not, this book is all about kissing. And while I'm not overly concerned with the conventions of genre, I'm amazed that anyone can consider this a fantasy.<br /><br />I should call this review: <b>Lies <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_" title="The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Deception</a> told me.</b><br /><br /><b>Lie #1: This book is fantasy.</b><br />If some very vague mentions of a kingdom and some very vague mentions of special powers add up to fantasy world-building for you, then you probably won't have a problem with this book. Because that is all you're going to get from this.<br /><br />I imagine some people will think I'm exaggerating when I say that this book really is all about the MC's boy issues, her maid's boy issues, and the boys in question, and we are supposed to imagine that there is a complex fantasy world existing in the background - but I am not exaggerating at all. If you thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> were fantasy-lite, then this is fantasy-zero (no sugar, no calories, tastes like ass).<br /><br /><b>Lie #2: Things actually happen.</b><br />No, they do not. The plot opens with Princess Lia escaping an arranged marriage along with her maid. The escape itself is also very vague because I guess it would be inconvenient to have to explain how a princess who is kept on a very tight leash manages to escape a supposedly heavily-guarded palace. <br /><br />She runs away to a little seaside town and becomes a waitress, does laundry and waits for her prince to come. No, really, there are pages and pages of this:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Putting the laundry up to dry didn’t prove any easier than washing it. After hanging a whole basket of sheets and standing back to admire my work, a stiff wind came along and sprang them all loose, sending my wooden pegs flying in different directions like mad grasshoppers.</i>
</blockquote><br />It was so so boring. And I bet you're still thinking I'm exaggerating and that there were actually things happening in the background (royal politics, drama, etc.) because of course this book can't really be about a waitress and a love triangle, right? Wrong!<br /><br /><b>Lie #3: Things make sense.</b><br />Firstly, the prince that Lia runs away from also felt tied to the marriage and didn't want it. So what does he do? He decides to go after Lia because she was brave enough to run away. What the fuck? Why is he following her? He got out of the marriage he didn't want!<br /><br />Secondly - wow, weird coincidence that the prince bumps into the assassin sent to kill Lia just outside of the inn where she's working. And they're both just like "hey, nice to meet ya, let's go for a pint". But this paves way for the dramatic moment when Lia looks up and - oh my! - two handsome strangers walk into the inn at the same time. I don't think it's meant to be amusing but it reminded me of that moment in <i>Mamma Mia</i> when the three dads all turn up at the same time. <br /><br /><b>Lie #4: There is an assassin.</b><br />Actually, the only thing killer about this assassin is his smirk. But really he's just a boy who can't do his job. He has hundreds of opportunities to assassinate Lia but he doesn't because he's too busy going googly-eyed and thinking about kissing her.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Hi face drew nearer, and I felt his breath on my skin. “I want to pull you close and never let you go,” he whispered.</i>
</blockquote><br />Sometimes enemy-turned-lover romances are hot but it's just a joke here because he DOESN'T EVEN TRY. Ever. Even in the beginning when he first meets her.<br /><br />There is only one truth told by this boring book and it's the title - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16429619.The_Kiss_of_Deception__The_Remnant_Chronicles___1_" title="The Kiss of Deception (The Remnant Chronicles, #1) by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Kiss of Deception</a>. It is, indeed, the perfect title. Because this book is deceiving and it's all about kisses.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“It’s not every day one has a first kiss,” I said.<br />“May I remind you that it wasn’t your first kiss?”<br />“It felt like it was. It was the first one that mattered.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12946406383725803358" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_879835235" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/879835235" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/879835235?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=best-main-characters">best-main-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=prince-and-princess">prince-and-princess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer879835235" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14119707211096133957"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406877745ra/10611208.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>What a beautiful and captivating story.</b><br/><br/>I’ve always had a soft spot for princess stories, true, but this one is like no other. Our lovely main character, Lia, wants free will…to fall in love with someone she actually knows and cares about. She is tired of always having her life decided, as princesses’ usually are, and the one thing she wants most, love, is up to her to find not for her father to plan. <br/><br/>For her to feel trapped no more, she escapes from her arranged marriage with someone who didn’t</span>
  <span id="freeText14119707211096133957" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406877745ra/10611208.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>What a beautiful and captivating story.</b><br><br>I’ve always had a soft spot for princess stories, true, but this one is like no other. Our lovely main character, Lia, wants free will…to fall in love with someone she actually knows and cares about. She is tired of always having her life decided, as princesses’ usually are, and the one thing she wants most, love, is up to her to find not for her father to plan. <br><br>For her to feel trapped no more, she escapes from her arranged marriage with someone who didn’t even take the time to see her before the event.<br><br>Now I’m not saying what she did isn’t reckless, since it <i>is</i> a kingdom and family she leaves behind, but I can certainly imagine how awful it must have been for her to grow up with an authoritarian parent and feel the need for freedom. Needless to say, I connected with Lia and felt quite invested in her story. <br><br>We have four different points of views in this story, but three are most present; Lia’s, The Assassin’s and The Prince’s. I couldn’t say which I preferred for they all fitted very well with the story and every character had something to say or makes us see, realize.<br><br>As for the love-triangle, I didn’t find it too heavy. In fact, the romance part of this story was present but not <i>too</i> much, which made me enjoy the story even more than I thought I would, surprisingly. I would love for her to end up with The Prince…but I could also see her spend her life with The Assassin. She could adapt to both ways of living, that’s for sure.<br><br>Many different characters are presented in this first book in a new series and they were all interesting. The only thing that I may have changed (or add in the sequels) is for them to be more present and described. Lia encountered some great people that I would hate for her to never see again.<br><br>Another thing that I loved was the setting. It’s not every day that we can read about a princess seeking shelter in a completely unexpected place, where no one would think of looking for her.<br><br>The writing was spectacular. It was so impressive and I completely fell in love with it. Every sentence or even description was flawless, in my opinion. What is strange is that, even though this story contains almost 500 pages, it felt much shorter. The pages flew by at a pretty fast speed. I was captivated the whole time and I wish for you to be as well, if you consider giving this book a chance.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14119707211096133957" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer762343976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11932947358999196088">An advance copy was provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br/><br/>This review can also be found at <a href='http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2014/06/review-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.<br/><br/>Review in a GIFfy -- This can also be found at <a href='http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2014/03/review-in-giffy-kiss-of-deception-by.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>. FULL REVIEW BELOW.<br/><br/>I must admit, I've never read a book by Mary E. Pearson. So when Kristen practically forced her copy on me (hehe), I was all:<br/><br/><a href='http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-xKe3UhAc7eA/UyYqiUpVl7I/AAAAAAAASbk/F0OmPoN0oPI/s1600/hmmokay.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031774.gif' height='180' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>And then I got to chapter 2, and it was on.<br/><br/><a href='http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-quWph6EUMQw/UyYrO0fDXRI/AAAAAAAASbs/aGR8QCdZ8X4/s1600/yougogirl.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031775.gif' height='168' width='320' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Not only is Lia fierce and determined not to be pushed into a marriage she does not desire, but her fr</span>
  <span id="freeText11932947358999196088" style="display:none">An advance copy was provided by the publisher in exchange for an honest review.<br><br>This review can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2014/06/review-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>.<br><br>Review in a GIFfy -- This can also be found at <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2014/03/review-in-giffy-kiss-of-deception-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Starry-Eyed Revue</a>. FULL REVIEW BELOW.<br><br>I must admit, I've never read a book by Mary E. Pearson. So when Kristen practically forced her copy on me (hehe), I was all:<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-xKe3UhAc7eA/UyYqiUpVl7I/AAAAAAAASbk/F0OmPoN0oPI/s1600/hmmokay.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031774.gif" height="180" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And then I got to chapter 2, and it was on.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-quWph6EUMQw/UyYrO0fDXRI/AAAAAAAASbs/aGR8QCdZ8X4/s1600/yougogirl.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031775.gif" height="168" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Not only is Lia fierce and determined not to be pushed into a marriage she does not desire, but her friend and lady's maid is just as awesome.<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-1reV5Kb6ToI/UyYsceMqIcI/AAAAAAAASb4/ufKXTZE4G34/s1600/bitchesgetstuffdone.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031776.gif" height="257" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don't know if Pearson always writes such strong-willed female characters, but I am impressed. Not just with those characters, though...with <i>everything</i>.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-k-HroXbzd2Q/UyYz6k-zryI/AAAAAAAAScI/xoR8gGyKEmk/s1600/ryanclapping.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031777.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The setting. The writing. The transitions between points of view. And there were several of them. All:<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-DBubA9_LD6o/UyY0z-Az9MI/AAAAAAAAScQ/yLRniJ_AnyE/s1600/exceptional.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031778.gif" height="136" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And as the story wore on, I found myself captivated, reading it anywhere and everywhere I could.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-uPIhG1cRDa0/UyY3kn5Y4WI/AAAAAAAAScc/AqO0EMVbi5w/s1600/captivatingread.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031779.gif" height="178" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then I found that I couldn't put the book down.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-3Ksu1U8nOy4/UyY3t0qJfOI/AAAAAAAASck/tq7Ci6pOqa4/s1600/babyreading.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031780.gif" height="234" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But when I got to page 300 or so:<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-zA6NrlaKZUM/UyY32ZSRwiI/AAAAAAAAScs/JeTmDI6y0vc/s1600/whatishappening.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031781.gif" height="223" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I did a bit of this:<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-UPBOVL3Sadc/UyY4Abe56sI/AAAAAAAASc0/8LI9zdE7Wg0/s1600/headache.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031782.gif" height="179" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then as I absorbed it all:<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Q1jk0VOAvcU/UyY4KkCPYMI/AAAAAAAASc8/v1KUCT5u_B8/s1600/brilliant.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031783.gif" height="183" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I can't say that the second half was lacking because my anticipation was still through the roof,<br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-2mI8Y70u5mk/UyY4gJnNkYI/AAAAAAAASdE/WetDT5RaxGo/s1600/icantwaittoseehowthisturnsout.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031784.gif" height="170" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>but it almost seemed like two separate stories after that point. Before: historical fantasy.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4z6nice24fY/UyY-JKBQVwI/AAAAAAAASds/7nmcR3R1-1k/s1600/brave.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031785.gif" height="158" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After: a quest-like fantasy, through the unyielding desert...<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-1BWecSaKlrk/UyY_2VtoN3I/AAAAAAAASd4/FEaKraOpjJU/s1600/desert.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031786.gif" height="176" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>with the possibility of some magic.<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ZMTyiw4OU3M/UyY5lmGLs1I/AAAAAAAASdM/wLg97Yd9EYs/s1600/ilovemagic.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031787.gif" height="180" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I say possibility because, well, I haven't seen any <i>true</i> magic yet. But I sense it.<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-rHqoAn408WY/UyY59z5bo7I/AAAAAAAASdU/2d7Vwzg2pdA/s1600/spideysenses.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031788.gif" height="176" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Other awesomeness:<br><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OFW8P8x-FWU/UyZAocAdk8I/AAAAAAAASeA/FouHUCP4FdA/s1600/gypsy.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697482ra/9031789.gif" height="144" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Gypsies<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-ZbgMdLG5t_Q/UyZBMqM96jI/AAAAAAAASeI/efE0IbJao6A/s1600/hunger-games-love-triangle-doodle.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395697482i/9031790.gif" height="223" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>A love triangle that isn't<br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XcOWm_kvL9Q/UyZC2WE3X3I/AAAAAAAASeU/nX82wuz8dys/s1600/logwrestling.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1395697482i/9031791._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Log wrestling...but with ruggedly handsome men over a mud pit  ;0)<br><br>All in all, this book was<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-8DI_3muIIxA/UyY6-F4IrkI/AAAAAAAASdg/Gc97EAinS64/s1600/fantastic.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1395697483ra/9031792.gif" height="152" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And I think that it ended at the best possible moment, even if the wait for the next book is going to kill me.<br>_________________________________<br><br>FULL REVIEW:<br><br><i>The Kiss of Deception</i> is actually my first experience with a Mary E. Pearson book. I think the science-y medical and ethical issues in the plot kept me away from <i>The Adoration of Jenna Fox</i> initially, but having taken a glimpse at the synopsis again, I can't really say exactly why. I love a good, introspective amnesia story, so I'll have to give that series a try soon, especially considering how much I loved this fantasy story from the author. And her characters. Gawd, those characters!<br><br>Lia is a formidable heroine. She is fierce and determined and willing to do the unthinkable to escape a life she does not want, including running from an arranged marriage. I can definitely get behind a protagonist like that, especially as she continues to grow over the course of the novel. She also has good taste in friends. Lia's lady's maid and dearest friend sticks with her through thick and thin, and she just may be the Princess's saving grace when all is said and done.<br><br>The first half of this novel spent a good deal of time introducing us to the characters and it felt more like a historical fantasy novel, which is pretty much what I expected based on the cover and the summary for the book. However, I did <i>not</i> expect the turn the novel would take about halfway through the story. The setting and the story abruptly changed, and it became more of a quest. But the transition to this aspect of the story and the deception that led there is handled phenomenally by the author. Things got a bit chaotic there for a bit, but I loved every second of it. It was shocking, surprising, and I found much of it to be entirely unpredictable, much to my own delight. The writing was just fantastic, and there was no way I was going to be able to put the book down after that.<br><br>This novel is actually rather brilliant. There's mention of magic but little to be seen of it. There's a day of sporting events that culminates in a bout of log-wrestling, which is just all kinds of genius. There are gypsies and vagabonds and vagrants of all sorts. And there is a bit of a love triangle that I didn't find distracting in the least because of how the characters are written. It does get a tad messy toward the end with no resolution, but that's the least of our girl's worries at that point. And I honestly don't think you should worry about the "love triangle" either because it's <i>mostly</i> nonexistent. Mostly.<br><br>At the heart of the story, I think the issue is who do you trust when no one is supposed to know who you are but practically everyone does? And moreover, most of those people aren't overly concerned with your well-being. Of course, Lia is unaware for most of the book that her life is in any <i>real </i>danger, though she knows there are people searching for her after she ran away from her wedding. That's probably the biggest deception of the story:  her perceived safety, especially when it comes to the two men who've worked their way into her heart. It's also one of my favorite aspects of the story:  not knowing who is who and what their intentions are.<br><br>It's books like this and <i>
  <a href="http://starryeyedrevue.blogspot.com/2014/02/review-winners-curse-by-marie-rutkoski.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse</a>
</i> that have reaffirmed my fanaticism for fantasy stories. I've read some real duds lately, but I think I'm finally out of that rut, thank goodness, thanks to books like these. Granted, I'm now craving some sequels like never before, but I survived the waiting with <i>The Girl of Fire and Thrones </i>series, and I know I'll survive this wait, too. (BTW, if you liked those books, you'll more than likely love this one, too. Just sayin'.) If you don't have this book on your TBR, you should remedy that immediately. It's full of adventure, romance, and betrayal, all of which obviously make it a captivating fantasy novel. I can't recommend it enough, and I'm actually already considering a re-read, if that tells you anything about my adoration for this book.<br><br>Be sure to check out my stop on the blog tour on July 7th!<br><br><b>GIF it to me straight:</b><br><a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/--7X2WI07WEM/U6CVAi2kJBI/AAAAAAAATmM/PRdor-rUMB8/s1600/amazing.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1403097946ra/10037809.gif" height="154" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Just absolutely phenomenal!</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11932947358999196088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1914378630" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914378630" />
    <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net"><img alt="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390032p2/7971097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1914378630?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914378630" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5311833124056995608"><b>This book is a triumph of its genre!</b><br/><br/>Okay, that may be overstating things <i>only slightly</i> (there were a couple of tiny things I took issue with) but I think it fair to overlook those small things in this case. Especially considering how <u>unfair, reactionary and very nearly malicious</u> I think some of the top-rated reviews for this book here on Goodreads are.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424653ra/846703.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Warning: strong opinions incoming!<br/><br/>I want to start out here by apologizing for what's to come.</b> I was a bit heated while I wrote it and tried to go </span>
  <span id="freeText5311833124056995608" style="display:none"><b>This book is a triumph of its genre!</b><br><br>Okay, that may be overstating things <i>only slightly</i> (there were a couple of tiny things I took issue with) but I think it fair to overlook those small things in this case. Especially considering how <u>unfair, reactionary and very nearly malicious</u> I think some of the top-rated reviews for this book here on Goodreads are.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380424653ra/846703.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Warning: strong opinions incoming!<br><br>I want to start out here by apologizing for what's to come.</b> I was a bit heated while I wrote it and tried to go back after a time and pare it down a bit so as not to offend. <br><br>It's just that I was so surprised when I finished this book and rushed to Goodreads to look through the reviews from the community only to find a spate of top-rated one star reviews awaiting me and every other person who ever looks this book up.<br><br><b>This is NOT a one-star book. </b> <br><br>To imply that it is when you have thousands of people who look to you for guidance should be criminal, or at the very least, frowned highly upon by the community at large and the people that actually did read this book.<br><br>I have to wonder as to the state of mind of that particular reviewer when they read it and reviewed it. Were they in a reading slump? Are they fans of the fantasy genre? Were they looking outside of their own personal feelings about love-triangles or female main characters as they read? Were they critically examining the structure of the prose when they determined that the book was only worthy of one star??<br><br><b>Were they considering the damage they do when they have a large following and rate a book that is well written but did not meet their own <s>personal preferences</s> expectations only one star?</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489953854ra/22265958.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>When I think of the thousands of readers out there that would otherwise have loved this book, but were turned off of it by these reviews, my heart literally aches. This is how we end up with 50 Shades of Grey and Twilight people! <br><br><b>This is how we get books devoid of emotion and heart.</b> Books that are poorly written and full of smirking love interests with smoldering eyes that have weak-ass main characters flopping back and forth between their convictions and their love of boys. Books that we have read a thousand times before and will read again.<br><br><i>It's one thing to DNF a book and make that clear within a concise review as to why the book just didn't work for you.</i> It's another thing entirely to deliver a scathing and extremely long review about said book to your thousands of followers and then point out at the very bottom in an offhanded manner that you didn't actually finish reading it after you've finished humiliating a person who took time and energy to write it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398352187ra/9404949.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I'm not saying that we can't all have opinions, or that this book is perfect, but to overlook ALL of the many positives within it and potentially turn off everyone who sees your review in the future is <u>so unfair to the author, the genre and the readers who follow you.</u> when there are WAY WORSE written books out there.</i><br><br><b>Yes, there's a love triangle in it but if we're being honest about it: It is <i>extremely</i> understated and this is also one of the rare cases in which a love triangle actually WORKS!</b> Those of you who know me, also know that I am the biggest opponent of love triangles in YA fiction. My last review actually railed against them completely. That being said, even I could bear the one here because it works so well within this story. Not to mention that it is almost fully resolved by the very end due to Lia's character arc.<br><br><b>And yes, Lia starts off in the cliche fantasy princess role, but lets also not overlook the fact that she experiences a ton of growth.</b> The character at the end of the book is entirely changed from the naive and idealistic teen she starts out as, and that's the point. The whole novel is proliferated by the thematic idea that events larger than ourselves destroy who think we are and change us into someone new. She had to start where she did or her arc wouldn't have worked.<br><br><b>But sure, lets rail against this book and give it one star because it has a princess in it.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449000400ra/17219089.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Also, the prose in this book is incredibly beautiful.</b> Pearson has such a command of language. Every word is included for a reason. It's flowery, but never to the point of becoming purple prose. Instead, each word works together to create a rich and beautiful world that I fell in love with. This is one of my favorite fantasy world I've read in recent months. <br><br>I see some of the reviews complaining that the book wasn't magical enough for fantasy, all the while overlooking the fact that Pearson, with her striking command of language and insidiously delivered worldbuilding talents was the true magician here.<br><br>The one thing I wanted more of in this book was more of a backstory for some of the ancillary characters around the 3 main characters, but I'm willing to overlook my own personal preferences in order to give this book a score that's a tad more realistic, if we're being honest.<br><br><b>★★★★★ = 4.5 stars &amp; a new favorite for me!</b><br><br>_______________________________<br>See this review, and more like it on my blog: <a href="https://bookbastion.wordpress.com/2017/03/19/review-the-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e-pearson/" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Bastion</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5311833124056995608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1061537580" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1061537580" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1061537580?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1061537580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7319872742361218219"><br/><b>
  <i>
    Imma need a mani after this book, because it sure was a nail bitter! Whoosh.
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Pretty sure by now you all know what the big hook of this book is; you have no idea who the assassin is and who the prince is. <i>I'll let you in on a little secret, I tried to guess and guessed wrong. </i><br/><br/>This story goes between switching Povs with Lia, Rafe, Kaden, the assassin, and the Prince. I'm becoming more and more a fan of switching views in stories, and this story is an added reason to why. Mary Pearson di</span>
  <span id="freeText7319872742361218219" style="display:none"><br><b>
  <i>
    Imma need a mani after this book, because it sure was a nail bitter! Whoosh.
  </i>
</b><br><br>Pretty sure by now you all know what the big hook of this book is; you have no idea who the assassin is and who the prince is. <i>I'll let you in on a little secret, I tried to guess and guessed wrong. </i><br><br>This story goes between switching Povs with Lia, Rafe, Kaden, the assassin, and the Prince. I'm becoming more and more a fan of switching views in stories, and this story is an added reason to why. Mary Pearson did an excellent job in seamlessly switching back and forth while leaving us little bread crumbs of evidence to which guy was which. Even with her little trails I was still guessing up until the last minute.<br><br>Now lets put our gloves on and really get down in it... Lia's character isn't a fighter but boy does she have a way with words. She is all sass all the time. Telling guys off is what she commands at. She does a lot of putting tough guys in their places, and I support this. She even threatens to have a few men become a little less manly if you catch my drift... <br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4Itt_ooe_Ls/VDXd-C8Qi-I/AAAAAAAAAHg/-7zWZiJeDg8/s1600/bada.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422668095ra/13532775.gif" height="161" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>There are several hints that ya girl may or may not have some kind of ancient super power... I say hint because it's never reviled if she does or doesn't. I love that Lia takes to working hard and not just laying around. I love that she's willing to give away everything at a chance to live a life of her own choosing. Even though there are a few times when her whole "which mysterious boy should I choose" thing gets a little overdone I can still stand behind her... That being said guess we should talk about that love triangle the story is based around. I both loved and hated it.<br>There's Rafe and then there's Kaden. Yup, That's pretty much all I can say about them without giving anything away... Oh but they are both super hotties! (swoon especially one of them *wink wink*) <i>Okay, okay I wont do that to you</i>, I'll try to give you a little more. <br><br>
  
    Both<br> boys made an impression on me right away. Rafe with his strength<br> and bold choices, and persistence. Then Kaden with his sweet ways and kind heart. <i>Now that I think about it I don't know if I would really call it a love triangle. I guess I would say they are both love interest.</i><br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-vKflIcBYDOE/VDa8J8yf0LI/AAAAAAAAAH8/aqCgGU84w5o/s1600/ht.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422668095ra/13532776.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>The second half of this book is <b>WAY </b>stronger than the first. Lia starts to really figure out who she wants to be and how she wants people to see her. There is a grave digging scene in this book and it's really what put me on team Lia. It is beautiful and probably my favorite part of the whole story. Now you're probably thinking "wtf? why is she digging a grave?!" THE SUSPENSE!!!<br><br>When things finally do start to come to light the story makes a really strong pull to the finish. Oh and of course I shouldn't fail to mention that <b>I loved the cliffhanger </b>and romance that wraps this story up!<br><br>There are two reasons I didn't give it a higher rating, 1) Is the cover. Yes it's beautiful BUT I hate when there's a person on the covers then they don't match the character descriptions. Lia is said it have dark hair and the girl on the cover has dirty blonde hair and 2) I felt at some point the writing was a little repetitive and felt like it was just used to fill up some space. Like sometimes less is more. Can't freaking wait to get a hold of book two
  
</span>
  <a data-text-id="7319872742361218219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1935896955" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1935896955" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1935896955?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=0-in-my-library-tbr">0-in-my-library-tbr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1935896955" class="readable"
              >

<span id="freeTextContainer3036893755866931431">This book is a re-read so I can continue on with the trilogy and I liked it the first time around but I loved it this time! Woot! <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497887569ra/23065913.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/>I loved this book, the atmosphere, the characters, the settings and the descriptions. <br/><br/>Lia is a strong character who decides she wants to live life her way and runs away with Pauline on her wedding day. Lia's family wanted to set her up in an arranged marriage to keep the peace, but it seemed to me they were already in a war regardless so I'm not sure how it would have</span>
  <span id="freeText3036893755866931431" style="display:none">This book is a re-read so I can continue on with the trilogy and I liked it the first time around but I loved it this time! Woot! <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497887569ra/23065913.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I loved this book, the atmosphere, the characters, the settings and the descriptions. <br><br>Lia is a strong character who decides she wants to live life her way and runs away with Pauline on her wedding day. Lia's family wanted to set her up in an arranged marriage to keep the peace, but it seemed to me they were already in a war regardless so I'm not sure how it would have played out. Lia had written a letter to the Prince for a meeting before their wedding, I think if this would have happened she would not have been so hateful about the idea, and of course, we wouldn't have had a book! <br><br>Lia and Pauline had a wonderful time working at an Inn/pub owned by Berdi. She didn't mind keeping the Princess hidden away as long as she worked etc. I loved the ambiance of the Inn/Pub and town. <br><br>There are assassins sent out after Lia and the Prince himself comes to find her. I was thinking the whole time, well he waits until she runs away to come to see her. Men! :) <br><br>So you have Rafe and Kaden, I wonder which one is the Prince. :) I loved them both but one more than the other. Swoon. Lol. There are other characters in the book that play good characters and bad characters. I thought they were all well played out. One of Lia's brothers, Walther, puts in a couple of appearances as well. I loved him! <br><br>There was a really sad part almost half-way through the book <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497887569ra/23065914.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And right at the end, an even more heartbreaking moment. I really hope Lia gets them all! She's strong, she can do this!<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/06/the-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e-pearson.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1674481795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3472369234063509982"><b>1.5 stars. </b><br/><br/>Watching my brother pick his nose would have been a more useful way to spend my time rather than on this pitiful excuse of a "fantasy" novel. If fantasy books are gross insta love with annoying as fuck love triangles and an assassin who can't get his job done because his little dick keeps getting in the way then I'm OUT. <br/><br/>You know, I actually liked the beginning. And I actually liked a little bit of the end. I just finished rewatching season 3 of TLA, which is why I was in a good mood,</span>
  <span id="freeText3472369234063509982" style="display:none"><b>1.5 stars. </b><br /><br />Watching my brother pick his nose would have been a more useful way to spend my time rather than on this pitiful excuse of a "fantasy" novel. If fantasy books are gross insta love with annoying as fuck love triangles and an assassin who can't get his job done because his little dick keeps getting in the way then I'm OUT. <br /><br />You know, I actually liked the beginning. And I actually liked a little bit of the end. I just finished rewatching season 3 of TLA, which is why I was in a good mood, but that doesn't excuse the rest of this boring, annoying, and absolutely petty plot. <br /><br />There's literally just a runaway princess who wants to start a fresh life and not be used in a political marriage and then she meets two guys who we need to figure out whether they're the prince or the assassin. And they both like her and she likes them too and then blah blah blah I stopped giving a fuck at that point because hey, <i>I don't fucking care about her lovey dovey love triangle issues!!</i> :)<br /><br />I was so worked up trying to figure out who was who. Was Kaden the assassin? Or was it Rafe? Was Kaden the prince? Or could Rafe be the prince? That held my attention for the first hundred or so pages but then *surprise* I couldn't find another fuck to give anymore!!! Because, nothing was happening!!! Nothing actually happens until the last couple of pages, which were also, *surprise* boring as fuck and *surprise* I didn't find a third fuck to give about it!!!<br /><br />Princess Lia is a character that was literally more duller and lifeless than my personality. My friends said that she goes through an amazing character development from the beginning to the end of the book, but I felt nothing?? I don't exactly hate her character, but I just feel nothing for her because she is literally so non existent to me. She's a ghost. <br /><br /><b>The assassin</b> was a big wimp. This guy was sent to kill Lia, but <i>wait</i>, his dick had other plans!!!! At first sight!!!!!!! An assassin sent to kill the girl, but falls in love with her?? Doesn't really sound that bad, actually! And the author could have pulled it off, but *surprise* the author chose insta lurveee and just no, goodbye. <br /><br />The prince was so bland as well. Well, all the characters actually, but he was even more pettier than the assassin!! Insta loveeeeeeeeee and no romance development and bye, off to the shark tank you go. <br /><br />I'm literally never following my dreams again because they just want me to read bad books and suffer. <br /><br />❌❌❌❌❌<br />I had a dream I read this series.<br /><br />Is this a sign???</span>
  <a data-text-id="3472369234063509982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_768752208" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/768752208" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/768752208?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=skulduggery">skulduggery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=i-hate-this-heroine">i-hate-this-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=assassins">assassins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer768752208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10145110829055895041"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2014/07/review-the-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e-pearson.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Let's talk about first impressions: they are IMPORTANT.<br/><br/>If, for example, you start reading a new book, and the first glimpses you get of ALL THREE main characters are less than flattering, you might be tempted to toss said book aside in disgust and hope the next one goes better.<br/><br/>Yes. You might.<br/><br/>And in this situation, I would not blame you. <br/><br/>So here's the deal: I'm not one of those the-less-romance-the-better types. I'm the opposite, in fact. In most cases, a book com</span>
  <span id="freeText10145110829055895041" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2014/07/review-the-kiss-of-deception-by-mary-e-pearson.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br>Let's talk about first impressions: they are IMPORTANT.<br><br>If, for example, you start reading a new book, and the first glimpses you get of ALL THREE main characters are less than flattering, you might be tempted to toss said book aside in disgust and hope the next one goes better.<br><br>Yes. You might.<br><br>And in this situation, I would not blame you. <br><br>So here's the deal: I'm not one of those the-less-romance-the-better types. I'm the opposite, in fact. In most cases, a book completely devoid of romance is a book I will almost certainly find lacking. That being said, I don't like romance tossed in willy nilly, b/c this book needs romance, so, "Hey! You two over there! Yeah, you! Make googly eyes at each other. I don't care if it doesn't make sense, just do it! Thaaaat's it, muuuuuchhh better."<br><br>In fantasy, one of the most common ways for romance to play out is the Arranged Marriage scenario. Neither party is happy about it, but something IMPORTANT is at stake, so two self-sacrificing souls agree to wed for the greater good. Then, despite the obvious unfairness of their situation, stuff happens, they fall in love, and they live HEA.<br><br>And this makes you happy, b/c SELF-SACRIFICE.<br><br>But what if Princess is a narcissistic little brat who not only runs away from her arranged marriage, but drags one of her good friends along with her? Who cares that the only way to ensure the safety of her family and the general population in the face of a barbarian invasion is to keep with tradition and unite her family with Prince's family, b/c NEITHER family has the strength to survive alone?<br><br>Not Princess. *frowns*<br><br>And not only does she not care, she laughs ALL THE TIME. Ah-ha-ha-ha laughs. Like Keira Knightley ruining Elizabeth Bennett in <em>Pride and Prejudice</em>. "Running away equals TREASON to my hard-case father, who had my cousin hanged for desertion, and buried him in an unmarked grave along with his mother (hard-case father's SISTER), who threw herself off a cliff in despair."<br><br>Ah-ha-ha-ha.<br><br>*flares nostrils*<br><br>Oh, and Prince only agrees to the marriage b/c his father tells him he can take a mistress.<br><br>And don't even get me started on Reluctant Assassin.&lt;------if you're going to be an assassin, you need to frickin' OWN IT.<br><br>BUT despite ALL of that, I kept reading. And it got better.<br><br>Nathan over at Fantasy Review Barn recently used the term "grab-bag" in one of his reviews, and I'm totally stealing it, b/c that's exactly what's going on here. We've got corrupt advisers to the monarch, a foreign, misunderstood queen who keeps IMPORTANT secrets from her daughter, gypsy caravans, a too-young soldier who bonds with his captive, a grizzled, veteran mentor, etc.<br><br>Oh, and there's also a TIGER. Can't forget about the (random) tiger.<br><br>So what's Princess doing now that she's the master of her own destiny?<br><br>Working at an inn as a barmaid. YEP. Freedom RAWKS. And it seems like she'd be content to stay there doing honest work forever, but that would be boring, so a Bad Thing happens that probably could have been avoided if she hadn't run away from her responsibilities, so of course she blames herself (b/c it's her fault), and she resolutely decides to return home, leaving behind the "farmhand" she's fallen in love with.<br><br>And it all goes downhill from there. The situation, not the story. The story, despite it's lack of anything new or original, is surprisingly entertaining, and I'll probably read the next book--who knows what bits and pieces will be thrown together in the next installment, right? <br><br>I'd recommend this book to anyone who isn't a termagant like I am, who thinks it's ridiculous to place the responsibilities of two kingdoms on the shoulders of a teenager.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10145110829055895041" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15955892261274249712" style="display:none">this is an excellent 'in the moment' kind of story. i felt super present and engaged whilst reading it, but i honestly havent really thought about this once since ive finished it... which makes me kinda wonder what i actually liked about it?<br /><br />im all for the whole runaway princess trope, but i wasnt really connecting with this particular princess. i really like both the assassin and the prince, but the ‘love triangle’ irritated me. the writing itself is pretty good, but the pacing is kinda slow and the story a little uneventful. the concept of people with gifts is interesting, but hardly any world-building explaining it is given. <br /><br />so some good and some bad. this book is adequate entertainment for what it is, but nothing that will most likely have a long-lasting effect on me. i may continue the series, but only because this ends on a cliffhanger.<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1157373040" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1157373040" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1157373040?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780805099232" href="/book/show/18490681-the-kiss-of-deception">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=unhauled">unhauled</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1157373040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5527682080919073474">I forgot how much I love fantasy and this book just sparked my desire to read more. I was captivated from page one. The writing of this book swept me off my feet and transported me to Lia's world. Everything was so vivid and encompassing and every emotion displayed was so relatable that I found myself deeply enjoying the story. Lia is such a great main character. She's strong and sassy unlike the generic YA heroine. Her wit and her class, combined with her capacity to feel such emotion came off </span>
  <span id="freeText5527682080919073474" style="display:none">I forgot how much I love fantasy and this book just sparked my desire to read more. I was captivated from page one. The writing of this book swept me off my feet and transported me to Lia's world. Everything was so vivid and encompassing and every emotion displayed was so relatable that I found myself deeply enjoying the story. Lia is such a great main character. She's strong and sassy unlike the generic YA heroine. Her wit and her class, combined with her capacity to feel such emotion came off extremely appealing to me because I was able to understand her, and I really respected every single thing she did in this book; she is a true heroine with golden intentions. I found the idea of this book to be extremely compelling, and although I enjoyed the first half's suspense better than the last half, the book was filled with emotion and surprises. The only reason I docked a star is because the fantasy aspects of this book are really underdeveloped. It outlines and hints at some sort of "power" that some people can have, but the reader is never told how that works, the history of who bears these powers, and what even the powers symbolize. It was all very confusing infused with old legends and explained in made-up languages, so I hope in the next books it becomes more clear about the powers!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5527682080919073474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
