              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=amazing-feelings">amazing-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=holy-shit">holy-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4858513-andreea-pop?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer893380315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10619271075799834469"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>Hello there, instant book obsession. <br/>Hello there, instant need for sequel.<br/>Hello there, instant love for Rafe and Kaden. <br/>I welcome you all with open arms, because I brought this upon myself by reading <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>. <br/><br/><a href='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-z6SGULAyPJE/VS1sRaly_oI/AAAAAAAAO1w/4VoLxAvF204/s1600/13153908.gif' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520641.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Gods above, this book is unputdownable deliciousness and it is totally worth the raves and hype. So this review won't exactly be a review -- my lips are sealed and my hands tied because I'd hate to give anything away from the glorious slow-burn and anticipation th</span>
  <span id="freeText10619271075799834469" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br><br>Hello there, instant book obsession. <br>Hello there, instant need for sequel.<br>Hello there, instant love for Rafe and Kaden. <br>I welcome you all with open arms, because I brought this upon myself by reading <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-z6SGULAyPJE/VS1sRaly_oI/AAAAAAAAO1w/4VoLxAvF204/s1600/13153908.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Gods above, this book is unputdownable deliciousness and it is totally worth the raves and hype. So this review won't exactly be a review -- my lips are sealed and my hands tied because I'd hate to give anything away from the glorious slow-burn and anticipation this novel sparks. I'll just be vague and I'll ramble and I'll gush and I'll fangirl. I probably won't even make much sense because I'm this close to turning into a pile of mush and I'd suggest you go with the flow and stop hunting for clues to why this book is awesome. It just is. Now I need to breathe. <br><br><i>
  <b>“Today was the day a thousand dreams would die and a single dream would be born.”</b>
</i><br><br>The aspect that told me that I'll have a fine time reading TKoD was actually its first line. Shattering dreams and forging new ones is my guilty pleasure and when a girl manages to accomplish that by fleeing on her wedding day, to say that I'm completely enraptured would be an understatement. <br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-SN_iQRo6_JY/VS1sTgWAOCI/AAAAAAAAO2Y/UAatKEydB60/s1600/tumblr_mmyhvlQ1M21sp9fcho1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520642.gif" height="167" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This girl is strong, compassionate and unyielding. Lia, as she likes to be called, is an independent and fierce young woman who happens to be the princess of The Kingdom of Morrighan being sent off to marrying Prince of Dalbreck, a neighbor-hooding land, to set an alliance. What happens from then on is a true testament to the girl's desire for free-will and simplicity. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-3H5lUoxfmb0/VS1sSrGwnQI/AAAAAAAAO2E/HOnZnYzqF9M/s1600/IMG_6339.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429040805i/14520643._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Her adventure is fascinating and it depicts wonderfully both the delightful and awe-inspiring elements Pearson has created in this universe, but also the sorrowful, darker and merciless ones. Coupled with an exquisite world-building that teases us with the lovely Terravin, hellish Cam Lanteux and everything in between, we are assured that the world portrayed is far from perfect and just, but also full of miracles, wonders and almost magical possibilities. <br><br><i>
  <b>“I see only reminders that nothing lasts forever, not even greatness.”<br>“Some things last.”<br>I faced him. “Really? And just what would that be?”<br>“The things that matter.”</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-_ilvFoqVAAM/VS1sTMzLV5I/AAAAAAAAO2o/466WKkirQMI/s1600/IMG_6341.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429040805i/14520644._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>In this regard, I have only words of approval. The spin on the fantasy the author wove through the plot sucked me right in with a teasing flavor that ensures the next installments will provide a fair amount of kick-ass developments in this area. At the same time, the mythology and historical background Pearson offered only amplified the feeling that the possibilities where this story could be taken are endless. I'm quite psyched to see what it is headed towards. <br><br>My one slight complain would be -- as obvious from my read stats -- the lack of action in the beginning. TKoD is the kind of read that keeps building and building (including the romance department, ahem) until a high note is achieved, leaving you awfully satisfied even though you didn't see a whole lot of fights and bloody corpses. The author throws you bits and pieces of violence and gut-wrenching scenes, enough to cut the story with cold, hard edges and imprint it with the necessary dangerous atmosphere. It still allows you to breathe and analyze, but somehow it traps you in and blocks every attempt at enjoying the book as a light, heartwarming story even though these nuances are present. It's still high fantasy, after all. <br><br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-Gz8vcK_hwjI/VS1sSXsyj1I/AAAAAAAAO2U/TJWZwMUK5kc/s1600/878108.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520645.gif" height="147" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The topic I've avoided and I'm certain you've been waiting for -- the romance. I'm sure you've heard some things about it as I'm sure you know there's a love triangle. There is, in fact, a love triangle and I'm going to bluntly say that it is brutal. Expect deception. Expect swoons. Expect secrets. Expect stomach butterflies and sighs. Expect sexiness and intensity.<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-YBUNFFdOdkc/VS1sRRWV44I/AAAAAAAAO14/xUMVgSk5GUo/s1600/10271680.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520646.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Expect everything, because with the plethora of twists (the holy shit kind; Bravo, Pearson!) you'll love both the boys vying for Lia's heart even if one of them will crush your heart in the process. The betrayal is bittersweet, somewhat understandable, because it tethers the line between love and duty and there's never an easy way to choose the one most powerful. <br><br><i>
  <b>“And if one can’t be trusted in love,” I added, “one can’t be trusted in anything.”</b>
</i><br><br>However, I did pick my favorite and I'm honestly intrigued how (or whether) the author will try to sway my opinion in the follow-up, since the tables have turned and the true faces behind the masks were unveiled, leaving us judging humanly flaws dead on, which is never an easy feat. <br><br><i>
  <b>“When I’m not with you, I wonder where you are. I wonder what you’re doing. I think about how much I want to touch you. I want to feel your skin, your hair, run every dark strand through my fingers. I want to hold you, your hands, your chin.” His face drew nearer, and I felt his breath on my skin. “I want to pull you close and never let you go”</b>
</i><br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-E_7lId7bUKU/VS1sSbqsrCI/AAAAAAAAO2A/c0XvFi7Uve0/s1600/IMG_6332.JPG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1429040805i/14520647._SY540_.jpg" height="320" width="243" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Some other aspects I'd like to applaud would be: the presence of strong, well-defined secondary characters I haven't expected -- especially Pauline; the bravery to kill us a little by making us love a certain character we haven't deeply explored in order to have the chance to do so chopped away; the balanced pace that, considering its lulls, allowed the plotline to move along nicely and, of course, the gorgeous capability of Mary E. Pearson of weaving such an enchanting tale. <br><br>Now I honestly don't know what I'm going to do until <i>The Heart of Betrayal</i> comes out in a few months. I'm quite obsessed. Consumed. Bewitched. An ARC would come in handy (am I being subtle enough?).<br><br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-HLF7oPyiKnQ/VS1sRXCHqOI/AAAAAAAAO10/nLZ1d4WNlZ8/s1600/663419.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429040805ra/14520648.gif" height="179" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Hopefully, you'll pick this book up and hopefully, you'll enjoy it as much as I did. <i>The Kiss of Deception</i> is a grand example of how a well-written novel can perfectly blend elements of original fantasy, electrifying love and thrilling stakes. In a game of hide and seek, there's a possibility you might get lost forever, but true beauty unravels when you fight with everything you've got to find the path where you belong, just like Lia -- and that's why my admiration for her story currently knows no bounds. <br><br><b>ENJOY! &lt;3</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10619271075799834469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1874654002" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1874654002" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1874654002?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22718798-the-kiss-of-deception">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1874654002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6231134782153455277"><b>"Who was this girl who thumbed her nose at two kingdoms and did as she pleased?"</b><br/><br/>It seems 2017 set out to be a year of surprises for me. And if all (most?) of them are going to be as pleasant and delightful as <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, bring them on.<br/><br/>•First of all, what I didn't expect was to be able to <b>connect with Lia</b>, our MC, so much and so <b>easily</b>. And, strange as it may seem, I don't feel like criticizing her for her decision to flee minutes before her wedding (no spoiler, it's all in the blurb):</span>
  <span id="freeText6231134782153455277" style="display:none"><b>"Who was this girl who thumbed her nose at two kingdoms and did as she pleased?"</b><br /><br />It seems 2017 set out to be a year of surprises for me. And if all (most?) of them are going to be as pleasant and delightful as <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, bring them on.<br /><br />•First of all, what I didn't expect was to be able to <b>connect with Lia</b>, our MC, so much and so <b>easily</b>. And, strange as it may seem, I don't feel like criticizing her for her decision to flee minutes before her wedding (no spoiler, it's all in the blurb): I was happy to see, for once, one heroine who dares take big risks simply for the sake of her own happiness, even though I can't deny that at that time she showed little care for her kingdom. But it was refreshing, in a way, and<b> I sympathized with her reasons completely, and found myself absolutely unable to blame her for her lack of selflessness</b>. In her shoes, I wonder, how many would have stayed, and how many would have fled? And if you stayed, would you do it because of your sense of duty, or because you'd be afraid of actually leaving behind the life you know? I, personally, think I would have listened to my cowardice and stayed. And if Lia had acted like this, giving in to fear, I would have liked her far, far less than, in fact, I did. So I wouldn't be so quick taking shots at her selfishness. <br /><br />•In spite of her being only seventeen, at times <b>her voice</b> (the novel is in the first person) was able to show a maturity that surprised me -but only at times; <b>chapter 31</b>, for instance, is an ode to every silly and insufferable female protagonist YA novels ever had. She flirts with one trying to anger the other, almost throws a fit when the other doesn't seem to care... bah. It's as if that chapter was taken from some other (and far more childish and idiotic) book and put in this one by some editorial mistake, which is completely implausible but still more likely than the alternative -the author gave in to a whim of hers that lasted too many pages. But don't worry, because, things go back to be awesome as if this chapter had never happened--or almost so: I would have avoided making them fight <i>Snow Like Ashes</i> (*gags*) style. But nothing too annoying, I promise you, and even if the characters and their actions/conversations have their naive and simplistic moments here and there, everything is very enjoyable and decidedly <i>not</i> over-the-top irritating.<br /><br />•For a bit more than half the book, <b>we don't know who's the assassin and who's the prince</b>! And the author showed great skill in <i>messing with our heads</i> and being able to lead us to think, basically, exactly what she wants us to believe. Which of course is the complete opposite of how things actually are! I think it is no mean achievement at all. Plus, <b>I had so much fun</b>, you really have no idea. <br /><br />•And <b>I ship them</b>! So much! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Lia and Rafe, I mean. Who else? Don't even think of Kaden, you hear me, Lia? NO Kaden!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />•Cherry on top, <b>the writing is utterly beautiful and enchanting</b>. Every sentence flows like music, like water. It won me over almost immediately.<br /><br />➽ I still have to read the next two books, obviously, but I don't think I'm exaggerating when I say that if the story stays this thrilling, and <b>if Lia keeps growing</b> like she did even in this first installment, <b>this could become one of my favourite series</b>. I'll try to keep my expectations at a reasonable level, but I admit that I want the next book to blow my mind.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6231134782153455277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2231641266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2231641266" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2231641266?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2231641266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3431684473409834910"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531420119ra/25965238.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> “It can take years to mold a dream. <br/>It takes only a fraction of a second for it to be shattered.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>Lia never wanted to marry a prince, she didn’t even get to meet him before the wedding. <br/>So she runs away, from her responsibilities and her own family, to a little town. <br/>There she starts to have a real life with her best friend Pauline.<br/>But our past always hunts us, and so two strangers appear. But who is who? <br/>Who’s the assassin, that needs to kill the runaway princess? <br/>And who is the</span>
  <span id="freeText3431684473409834910" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1531420119ra/25965238.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> “It can take years to mold a dream. <br>It takes only a fraction of a second for it to be shattered.” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Lia never wanted to marry a prince, she didn’t even get to meet him before the wedding. <br>So she runs away, from her responsibilities and her own family, to a little town. <br>There she starts to have a real life with her best friend Pauline.<br>But our past always hunts us, and so two strangers appear. But who is who? <br>Who’s the assassin, that needs to kill the runaway princess? <br>And who is the prince who wants to see his runaway bride-to-be? <br>I really really liked this book. It wasn’t a five star read, it had too much romance in it, but it was still filled with a brilliant world building, secrets to unfold and enemies that could be friends and friends that could betray you. <br><br>Character ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> „Sometimes the enemy is just one person who will bring down a kingdom.“ </i> <br>We meet a main character, who is fierce and strong and has a stubbornness in herself, that’s filled with love for others, but also herself. She has a healthy self-consciousness and knows what is right or wrong. <br>But still she makes mistakes, and that is fine. She’s young after all, in a far away small town filled with strangers. <br>I especially liked her talent with languages. The Vendan language was so fascinating, I would love to speak it myself! <br>It’s just filled with so much mystery. <br>Kaden was by far my favorite male character. He has a soft side of him, the kind eyes and mercy. But he was still strong and loyal. <br>Rafe was kind of the bad guy in this story. He was a little bit mean and sometimes he didn’t say the right thing. But again, that’s fine. We’re all not perfect. And Rafe isn’t either. <br>Pauline and the others were a little bit plain, but I guess that is normal when you’re a side character that is mostly there for support. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> „Once upon a time, there was a man as great as the gods…<br>But even the great can tremble with fear.<br>Even the great can fall” </i> <br>Morrighan and Dalbreck were never good friends or neighbors. They always had their difficulties. But they had one thing in common - Venda, a place filled with barbaric people, their enemies.<br>Every country has their own history, but if they all share one part - are they really that different from each other? <br>This was by far the best thing of the whole book. The author created different countries and different languages with a touch of mystery in their history. <br>If this was real life I would probably love to be a Vendan. Or a princess in Morrighan. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️<br><i> „Maybe there was no one way to define it. Maybe there were as many shades of love as the blues of the sky,” </i> <br>Ladies and gentlemen, I present you - a love triangle. 👏🏻🙈 <br>Who will she pick? The nice and gentle one or the one that’s mean and a little bit rough sometimes? Will she pick the one that is kind or the one that is a bit mysterious?<br>You know what? Who cares. <br>I wanted to see how the story continues. <br>And I saw, and I liked it. <br>So, I’m not a fan of the love interest, but it was okay. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><i> „Today was the day a thousand dreams would die and a single dream would be born.” </i> <br>In this one we have three POVs, in the end four. Between the POVs of the characters, there were snips of the history of Morrighan, Dalbreck and Venda. Songs, words from a diary and poems. <br>It was beautiful, even though the writing itself could’ve been better. <br><br>______________________________________________________<br><br>Buddyreading with one of the nicest and funniest guys on Goodreads :)<br><br>So excited for this book!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1526072892ra/25525287.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3431684473409834910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1903246994" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903246994" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903246994?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/22718798-the-kiss-of-deception">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1903246994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14942422132119300261">Buddy reading with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cait</a>!! <br/><br/>Do you hear that? Yes, it's the sound of me crying because I am disappointed. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong, this wasn't a bad book, I was just expecting <i>so much more</i>. I was expecting to be blown away. Oh well. Expectations are the worst, let's be real.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“It can take years to mold a dream. It takes only a fraction of a second for it to be shattered.”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>As the blurb states, princess Lia escapes the day of her arranged wedding because she doesn't want to abide by traditions and she d</span>
  <span id="freeText14942422132119300261" style="display:none">Buddy reading with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait</a>!! <br /><br />Do you hear that? Yes, it's the sound of me crying because I am disappointed. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, this wasn't a bad book, I was just expecting <i>so much more</i>. I was expecting to be blown away. Oh well. Expectations are the worst, let's be real.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“It can take years to mold a dream. It takes only a fraction of a second for it to be shattered.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />As the blurb states, princess Lia escapes the day of her arranged wedding because she doesn't want to abide by traditions and she doesn't want to marry someone she doesn't know. As she's adapting to her new life, she meets two guys, Rafe and Kaden, one of them is an assassin sent to kill her and the other is the prince she was supposed to marry; however, <u>we don't know who's who.</u> We have to find out the identities of who's who. I actually enjoyed searching for clues to find out who's who, and I had the wrong theory until a few chapters before the reveal. <b>Well played, Mary E. Pearson, well played!</b><br /><br />The main problem with this book was the plot: there was no plot. For the first 60% of the book, nothing of importance was going on, hence I got easily distracted. The only thing going was the mystery of Rafe and Kaden's identities, which was revealed at precisely the 65% mark. Only after I reveal, the plot began and I really started enjoying the book more and actually caring for the events and the characters. If it hadn't been for the mystery of the identities keeping me going, I would've gave up.<br /><br />Yes, there is a love triangle, which for me, was light. It didn't bother me greatly. I wasn't too invested in it anyway. I definitely like Rafe way more than Kaden; both as separate character and as a love interest. I don't really care for Kaden. <br /><br />Anyway, despite not overly enjoying this, I will still continue on with the trilogy because I'm really interested to see where this will go. I'm actually pretty excited too! I've also heard that book two gets way better. I hope so!<br /><br /><b>Pre-review:</b><br /><br />I will cry if this doesn't turn out good, okay. I <i>need</i> this to be good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14942422132119300261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1960707982" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1960707982" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1960707982?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=royal-binches">royal-binches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=shippity-ship-ship">shippity-ship-ship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=period-aus-past">period-aus-past</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=high-dark-epic-fantasy">high-dark-epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66222749-booksnpenguins?shelf=book-heaven">book-heaven</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1960707982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5876254164498536787">excuse me while I have a heart attack.<br/><br/>There are books and then there are <i>books</i>.<br/>For me, The Kiss of Deception belongs to the second category.<br/>I can’t pinpoint exactly what it is about this book that got me so hooked (and right from the start, dare I say), because, let’s be honest, there are better, and better written stories, out there. <br/>But there is something, something I can’t explain with words, that inevitably made me love every single line and scene, every single page and twist.<br/>The Kiss of Dec</span>
  <span id="freeText5876254164498536787" style="display:none">excuse me while I have a heart attack.<br><br>There are books and then there are <i>books</i>.<br>For me, The Kiss of Deception belongs to the second category.<br>I can’t pinpoint exactly what it is about this book that got me so hooked (and right from the start, dare I say), because, let’s be honest, there are better, and better written stories, out there. <br>But there is something, something I can’t explain with words, that inevitably made me love every single line and scene, every single page and twist.<br>The Kiss of Deception is a pretty much fast-paced story of a princess who decides to take her life in her own hands and do something for herself, for once. And here she does it, mainly because she can’t bear the thought of marrying someone she doesn’t love, someone who’s spineless enough to not react to an arranged marriage. <br>Imagine being that pure-hearted. Can’t relate, but I totally admire her for this.<br>Lia is one of the best female characters I’ve read about, lately. She’s flawed, stubborn, still not at her peak of matureness, and she’s definitely not another ass-kicking, shade-throwing, chosen one, but she knows her stuff. Oh, boy, does she know it.<br>What I like about Lia the most is how strong she is. Emotionally, spiritually, she’s a rock, and she’s clever enough to understand when it’s time to shut up and back off for the sake of her own and other people’s safety and well-being (yes, America Singer, this one was for you).<br>She always thinks about others first (especially her brothers and her friends), and she’s not afraid of getting her hands dirty. And it’s not like she always succeeds in doing whatever she has in mind, but she puts all herself in what she does.<br>If anything, one must appreciate her even only for her effort. <br>Another thing I adored about this story, is the female bonding. It is so strong in this book, and it’s literally everywhere. There are great, well developed and relatable female characters all over the book. It’s a pleasure to see them interact with one another, it’s even more wonderful to see how, for these women, their friendship and girl bond, always comes first. They’re all role models kind of characters (without losing their mysterious aura, like in Gwyneth’s case, or gaining even a motherly touch as it happens with Berdi and Dihara), flaws and all.<br>In general, the character dynamics were great and remarkable, for what it comes to established relationship (Lia and Pauline, Rafe and Sven, for example), and for the ones formed page after page (Lia and Berdi is hands down my favorite one. I freaking love Berdi, I won’t tell this enough).<br>As for the romance part…Would you believe me if I told you that I love this book so much I don’t even care that there’s a <s>very unnecessary why would you do this to my poor heart</s> love triangle squeezed there somewhere? Sure, there were moments where I’d rather have flushed this book down the toilet, but, hey, angst is the spice of life.<br>At leaest there are only two love interests (are you familiar with the <i>House of Night</i> series? I’ve never met another protagonist who has that many lovers and crushes, I swear to god, it gets almost embarassing at some point), and they were both super duper likeable. A bit cheesy, at times (especially Rafe; like, my boy is so smitten how is he even that whipped), but surely not a sickening kind of cheesy.<br>I think everyone on here, by now, knows where my preferences stand, but I must admit I didn't mind the "rival" at all (still, SORRY KADEN, BUT RAFE ALL THE WAY); also, the switching POVs kinda help getting sympathetic towards both of them, not to mention how nice it is to see the story from another perspective. <br>Our two young bucks, in addition, both love Lia for the right reasons (and how could they not love her? I too have a huge crush on her T___T). They know her worth, they know she’s not just a damsel in distress -because she clearly isn’t-, they know she’s not another spoiled brat ready to play games on them, and, all above this, they definitely know she could kick them both in the junk if she knew that they’re planning on doing something she’s not fond of. <br>Plus, no, Lia doesn’t spend pages and pages crying and whining over how much she loves this but oh, how much she also loves that. Well, not that much at least, but she’s still seventeen, pretty, young, and free to do whatever she pleases for the first time in her life. She’s allowed to be confused and flirty, okay? A love triangle is almost forgivable under these conditions. But again, I said ALMOST.<br>Now, about the fantasy factor: I think the whole First Daughter thing portaits again how much this book chersishes and values the importance of women, and I couldn’t be more happy about it. All the legends about Morrighan and the Remnant and Venda and the vagabonds (I loved that part so much??? It was so evocative!) were interesting and they were absolutely necessary to the whole world building thing, especially if you consider how much stories and ancient mysteries are important to the plot.<br>I also need to know more about Lia’s gift. Me curious.<br>The writing is nice, clear, fluent and straight to the point; nothing extraordinary or too elliptical, but I’ve never witnessed dull moments or scenes where I had to reread phrases more than once like it happens sometimes with this kind of books. There weren’t many quotable lines, but the exquisitely written dialogues totally compensated.<br>There also were moments where I found myself on the verge of tears or with a pounding heart. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The scene where Lia witnesses the murder of her brother and then buries his and his soldiers’ bodies, for example. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> That one made me sob hard.<br>Also, I’m a huge sucker for languages and I think the author knew what she was doing on that part, that is, adding to the story a foreign language the protagonist learns little by little, and the reader as well, along with her.<br>And, oh, nice touch with the whole <i>The Prince/The Assassin-Who is Who</i>, thing. I’m looking at you, Mary E. Pearson, and I’m winkwinking. Hard. <br>You almost got me there.<br>I've also had a lot of fun fancasting all the characters. I am all in for Adelaide Kane as Lia. She's perfect. A bit too old, maybe, but can a girl dream? I think she can. <s>And I also think she's allowed to fancast Torrance Coombs as Rafe and IT SURELY HAS NOTHING TO DO WITH ALL THE ALREADY MADE GIFS ONE CAN EASILY FIND ON THE INTERNET.</s><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/bS8E" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492705857ra/22544259.gif" alt="tumblr_muwofsqx0o1sn21e9o3_500_zpsf72fbfe9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>In conclusion, I can’t wait to read more about Lia and the others, just like I can’t wait to see where this is all headed, and I think the reason is because the writer did an awesome job by not giving away too much on this first book. <br>What’s gonna happen to Lia? Will she ever return to Morrighan? What will happen to her and Rafe?<br> What's the Chancellor hiding? And what's the deal with those Vendans books? And what about Pauline? AND WHAT ABOUT THAT TATTOO??? Too many questions, too little time to answer them all.<br>I’m totally craving for more. More Lia, more Rafe, more Pauline and Kaden, more legends, more love, more everything.<br>*throws confetti* YAY FOR THE KISS OF DECEPTION!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5876254164498536787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2222331525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12231182886557576834"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515341004ra/24853798.gif' width='500' height='281' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So, after I struggled for days to read this book, I finished it in one sitting. I just love my poor decisions in life.<br/><br/>The first have of the book was hard for me to read -it was slow and, while fun, kind unimpressive. And I liked Lia and Pauline, they were cool to read and their adventures as they went undercover and worked at the inn.<br/><br/>I also thought I was not going to like the whole main attractive of the book -the two boys sent after Lia, the prince and the assassin. I was not in for the love tr</span>
  <span id="freeText12231182886557576834" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515341004ra/24853798.gif" width="500" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, after I struggled for days to read this book, I finished it in one sitting. I just love my poor decisions in life.<br><br>The first have of the book was hard for me to read -it was slow and, while fun, kind unimpressive. And I liked Lia and Pauline, they were cool to read and their adventures as they went undercover and worked at the inn.<br><br>I also thought I was not going to like the whole main attractive of the book -the two boys sent after Lia, the prince and the assassin. I was not in for the love triangle and yeah, there were parts of it where I was ready to bash my head into the wall but most of the time I wasn't overwhelmed by it. I liked both boys differently and the reveal, though not a big surprise, was good to the plot.<br><br>Overall I enjoyed this book way more than what I thought I was going to and now I'm excited for book 2 and read what Lia is really going to be like. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12231182886557576834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1795488187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1795488187" />
    <a title="Camile Souza (This Chamber of Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5281575-camile-souza-this-chamber-of-books"><img alt="Camile Souza (This Chamber of Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345182316p2/5281575.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1795488187?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Camile Souza (This Chamber of Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Camile Souza (This Chamber of Books)" href="/user/show/5281575-camile-souza-this-chamber-of-books">Camile Souza (This Chamber of Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Camile by: </span>
      Stephanie Garber
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5281575-camile-souza-this-chamber-of-books?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5281575-camile-souza-this-chamber-of-books?shelf=tbr-2017">tbr-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1795488187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2570043224538069268">Utter <i><b>disappointment</b>.</i><br/><br/>Sheer <i><b>frustration</b>.</i><br/><br/>That's what I felt when I finished reading this book. Now here's a <b>
  <i>*rant*</i>
</b> on why.<br/><br/>To me <i>
  <b>The Kiss of Deception</b>
</i> started off <i>boring</i> and it remained <i>really boring</i> for the first <b>200 pages</b> ugh. <b>Nothing interesting really happened</b>, I felt no excitement <i>whatsoever</i>, and I have <i>no idea</i> why the author felt the need to tell us ALL ABOUT <b><i>Lia</i>'s daily chores</b> for so <i>damn</i> long. I read fantasy for <i>escapism</i>, so if I wanted to read all about someone <b>doing <i>regular</i> laundr</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2570043224538069268" style="display:none">Utter <i><b>disappointment</b>.</i><br /><br />Sheer <i><b>frustration</b>.</i><br /><br />That's what I felt when I finished reading this book. Now here's a <b>
  <i>*rant*</i>
</b> on why.<br /><br />To me <i>
  <b>The Kiss of Deception</b>
</i> started off <i>boring</i> and it remained <i>really boring</i> for the first <b>200 pages</b> ugh. <b>Nothing interesting really happened</b>, I felt no excitement <i>whatsoever</i>, and I have <i>no idea</i> why the author felt the need to tell us ALL ABOUT <b><i>Lia</i>'s daily chores</b> for so <i>damn</i> long. I read fantasy for <i>escapism</i>, so if I wanted to read all about someone <b>doing <i>regular</i> laundry</b> and <b>waiting <i>ordinary</i> tables</b>... <i>Oh wait</i>, why exactly would I want to do that?<br /><br />Maybe if I were raised in <i>privilege</i> I could've understood <b>Lia</b>'s fascination with doing these <b><i>mundane</i> chores</b> <s>not really though</s>, but I still wouldn't understand why <i>on earth</i> we were spending so much <i>freaking</i> time watching her do them. <b>Where the hell is my <i>escapism</i></b>?<br /><br />Or perhaps, if I had actually <i>seen</i> more of <b>her life in the castle</b> before (and even after) she ran away, instead of having her <b>
  <i>'telling'</i>
</b> me all about how people were so <i>unfair</i> to her, and how she was so much <i>smarter</i> than them, and how her life was sooo <i>horrible</i> because <b>they treated her like a <i>princess</i></b>, then sure, maybe I could've understood her. <i>*queue the sarcasm*</i><br /><br />Let me tell you, <b>Lia</b> and I began with the <i>wrong</i> foot.<br /><br />Right at the beginning she says that she is being forced to get married with the prince of <i><b>Dalbreck</b>,</i> a man she doesn't even know. That sucks, right? For sure, but also, it shouldn't be such a shock since <b>her own mother had an arranged marriage</b> with her father. But I get it <i>
  <b>Lia</b>
</i>, you have the right to not be happy with that.<br /><br />Okay, but then she goes on to explain, that this is not just some random power hungry move from her father. Her kingdom, <i><b>Morrighan</b>,</i> actually <i>needs</i> an alliance with <i>
  <b>Dalbreck</b>
</i> in order to survive an attack from <i><b>Venda</b>,</i> a wilder and bigger kingdom. Now, she mentions <i>
  <b>Morrighan</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>Dalbreck</b>
</i> do <b>NOT</b> get along, so wouldn't one think that these two countries who really dislike each other would not <i>choose</i> to solidify an alliance through marriage, unless <i>
  <b>Venda</b>
</i> was a real threat and that if this alliance didn't happen the other option would likely be go to war? And if that's the case, shouldn't the <i>princess</i> who is about to be wed, at least <b><i>think</i> about the consequences</b> to her <b>people</b>, to her <b>family</b> and to her <b>friends</b> if she ignored this and just ran away?<br /><br />Also if she <i>knows</i> that what she did is considered <i>treason</i> and <b>punishable by <i>death</i></b>, shouldn't she <i>at least</i> show a bit more <i>concern</i> about <b>what would happen to the <i>friend</i> who helped her escape</b> if they ever got caught? She'd certainly be <b><i>extra</i> careful</b> to make sure that wouldn't happen, right? <i>Right?</i><br /><br />I'm not even saying that she shouldn't have ran away. The whole premise of the book comes from that, it's <i>fine</i>. But <b>what <i>REALLY</i> rubbed me the wrong way</b> was that she didn't even stop to <i>consider</i> what would happen to other people <b>because of her actions</b>. Like <b>wtf</b>, your country could go to <i>war</i> because of what you did and you're like <i><b>"peace off bitches</b>, I'm just gonna go chill as a waitress and flirt with some random dudes ok bye".</i> Right, because that's not <i>selfish</i> at all.<br /><br />If she really is <i>smarter</i> than everyone in the castle as she likes to claim, I must say that <i>
  <b>Morrighan</b>
</i> is really <i>doomed</i>.<br /><br />Ohh when you don't get along with the <i>main</i> character, it's really hard to enjoy a book that is mostly from their perspective <s>and that girl is such a damn <i>princess</i> it's hilarious when other characters act like she's <b>"not like other court girls"</b> just because she wears pants and wait tables</s>, especially since not many exciting things happen. But <b>Lia</b> was not alone in my <i>distaste</i> for her.<br /><br />- <i>
  <b>The Prince</b>
</i> and <i>
  <b>The Assassin</b>
</i> <i>*sighs heavily*</i><br /><br />Okay, let's start by saying it, <b>THEY DO NOT MAKE ANY SENSE AT ALL</b>. The <b>prince</b>, who <b>did NOT want to get married</b> to some princess he'd never met from a kingdom that was <b>not</b> friendly to his, finds out that said princess <i>ran away</i> from the wedding, therefore <b><i>releasing</i> him from an obligation he did NOT want</b>. Great, he's free now. But then what does that <i>prince</i> do, even though <i>nobody</i> asked him to? He immediately decides to <b>hit the road</b> <i>by himself</i> to spend <i>days</i> tracking the aforementioned <b>runway bride</b> who <b>he did <i>NOT</i> want to marry</b> in the first place. One could think "oh even though he didn't <i>want</i> to marry her, he must've thought that he <i>should</i> do this because of his duty to his country". Lol not really, his justification was actually <i>
  <b>"I want to meet this girl who had the courage to do what I wanted to, but couldn't"</b>
</i>. I mean???<br /><br />Sure, that's obviously <i>very</i> <b>logical behaviour</b> and not <i>creepy</i> at all "hey I didn't even <i>know</i> you, and I didn't <i>want</i> to marry you, but now that you <i>rejected</i> me I'm going to spend my days <i>tracking</i> your ass down."<br /><br />And <b>the assassin</b>. Oh the <i>assassin</i>. I must congratulate him because he is certainly one of the <b>most <i>incompetent</i> assassins</b> I've ever read about. You are sent to this kingdom with the <i>important mission</i> to <b>track and kill someone</b>, because that's your <i>job</i>. You claim to have done it many times. Then you locate your target, <b>a silly runaway princess</b> who poses no threat to you - but <b>who could be a threat to your kingdom</b> if she marries an enemy prince -, it might not be a <i>pleasant</i> job, but it's not a <i>difficult</i> one either, at least not for <i>you</i>, an <i>experienced</i> assassin. <b>You've done it before</b>, and you <i>know</i> you're gonna kill her, because you can't go home otherwise. So what do you do? <i>OF COURSE</i> you decide to <b><i>procrastinate</i> for weeks to flirt and get to know your target instead of eliminating her right away</b>. Like, whaaat? I mean, it feels like he falls in love with this girl because he was <i>too lazy</i> to kill her. If this were his first job, then okay I'd give him a pass, but he's done this <i>many times</i> before, so really dude?<br /><br />Now, I don't know what was the deal with it, but the <b>
  <i>writing</i>
</b> in this book did <b>NOT</b> work for me. I found myself <b>wanting to skip <i>entire</i> paragraphs of descriptions</b> because they were just <i>filling</i> the page. I also wish there were more lines of <b><i>direct</i> dialogue</b> between the characters, instead of having <b>
  <i>Lia</i>
</b> constantly <i>tell</i> me "I did this", "we talked about that", "we fought many times".<br /><br />I mean, what has more <b>emotional <i>impact</i></b>? When you're <i>
  <b>shown</b>
</i> two characters <i>yelling</i> lines of <i>
  <b>actual dialogue</b>
</i> at each other so you can <i>feel</i> the punch of what they're saying, or when the narrator/character simply <i>
  <b>tells</b>
</i> you <i>"We argued loudly"?</i><br /><br />It's the old <b>
  <i>"show - don't tell"</i>
</b> thing. If you just <i>tell</i> me stuff, I'm not likely to <i>feel</i> like I'm <i>seeing</i> the story unfold. Instead I'm only <i>hearing</i> some <i>third party</i> talk about how <i>they</i> thought things went on. I'm not <i>there</i> myself. <b>I felt like an <i>outsider</i> throughout this whole book</b> and that was horribly <i>frustrating</i>.<br /><br />I also did not really care much for any of the <b>characters</b>, and I felt the <b>worldbuilding</b> (even though it had some cool ideas) <b>was quite <i>shallow</i></b>, especially where it shouldn't, like, huh, <b>politics</b>? I'm not even talking complex politics here, I think it failed at the very basics of it. And boy, <i>oh boy</i> <b>did we take our time to get out of <i>Terravin</i></b>. I mean, the girls ran away and just <i>stayed</i> there like <i>foreeeeever.</i> We only got to know like <i>one</i> interesting place after leaving that <i>godforsaken</i> village. This did not feel like a world I'd have any interest in visiting, or even like a <i>world</i> at all.<br /><br />Oh btw how damn <i>easy</i> it was for people to find <b>Lia</b>. Like wow, <i>fanstastic</i> job at hiding.<br /><br />Anyways, the way the story was written, most things ended up feeling so <b>impersonal</b> and <b>emotionless</b> to me. I got so <i>frustrated</i> for not being able to <i>care</i> about things. It might not seem like it, but <b>I <i>REALLY</i> wanted to enjoy this book</b>. I kept on hoping things would get <i>better</i>, and they kinda did eventually, but only to go <i>downhill</i> again later.<br /><br />Part of me still wants to read the rest of the triology, simply because <b>I don't like quitting things</b> (I'm a <i>masochist</i> apparently), and also people say the second book is better. But the same people loved this first book, while I do not have any good feelings about it. Their "better" might not be the amount of <b>"betterness"</b> I'd need to get some enjoyment out of it. Maybe I just feel the need to understand <b>what is it about this <i>damn</i> triology that so many people</b> I know (and usually have similar tastes with), <b>find so <i>praiseworthy</i></b>.<br /><br />I mean, if you liked this book, good for you, truly, because I'd never wish on anyone the same feelings I had while reading this. Yikes!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>*end of rant*</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /><a href="https://thischamberofbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/CamileSouza" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/camilesouza/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3604297218" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3604297218" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606141536p2/114413220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3604297218?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=failed-romance">failed-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=strong-female-protagonist">strong-female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=well-that-was-a-cheap-plot">well-that-was-a-cheap-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=your-typical-ya-fantasy">your-typical-ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=how-was-this-published">how-was-this-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=love-geometry">love-geometry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=stock-side-characters">stock-side-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=what-a-pointless-book">what-a-pointless-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3604297218" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15586464037342537031">When someone shoves a book in my face and tells me it's high fantasy, I expect a few things.<br/><br/>1. A thought-out plot<br/>2. Worldbuilding<br/>3. Characters with brains<br/>4. Good writing<br/><br/>According to my checklist, this book is not a high fantasy. It's a.... *checks notes* hastily put-together, jumbled mess of trite tropes traditionally categorized as fantasy. So.<br/><br/><br/><b>1. A thought-out plot</b><br/><br/>Princess Lia, terrified of being forced into an arranged marriage, runs away to live a peaceful life by the sea. Because no one will</span>
  <span id="freeText15586464037342537031" style="display:none">When someone shoves a book in my face and tells me it's high fantasy, I expect a few things.<br><br>1. A thought-out plot<br>2. Worldbuilding<br>3. Characters with brains<br>4. Good writing<br><br>According to my checklist, this book is not a high fantasy. It's a.... *checks notes* hastily put-together, jumbled mess of trite tropes traditionally categorized as fantasy. So.<br><br><br><b>1. A thought-out plot</b><br><br>Princess Lia, terrified of being forced into an arranged marriage, runs away to live a peaceful life by the sea. Because no one will be able to track her. Not even the King's soldiers. And obviously no one in the peaceful town by the sea knows what the missing princess looks like. Nothing about this plan could go wrong. Nothing... at all... <br><br>Enter the Prince and the Assassin, who just happened to show up at the same peaceful town by the sea, *the convenience is painful* searching for Lia. The Prince isn't old or decrepit like she was afraid of - he's handsome (oh wow, who would have ever thought). Lo and behold, the Assassin isn't too bad to look at, either! Could... there be... a love triangle? Could... both men... fall in love with Lia? *suspense* <br><br>This is the plot up to 15%. And after that, here's what happens. <br><br>1. Lia does laundry<br>2. Lia chops onions<br>3. Lia bemoans her fate, because how could she possibly choose between the prince and the assassin? There are definitely no other, more important things to worry about. <br><br>I'm not joking. This is the entire plot after 15%. *sigh*<br><br><br><b>2. Worldbuilding</b><br><br>This is supposed to be fantasy. I think. But there's no worldbuilding; just a vague semblance of it. <br><br>What I'm given is a bunch of random terms shoved in my face. Of which I remember approximately zero. Because there's no context at all, just names. One might have thought a fantasy novel needed a world... <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1603197168ra/30262303.gif" alt="Hahaha No GIFs - Get the best GIF on GIPHY" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>3. Characters with brains</b><br><br>The characterization in this book is sooo sloppy. It's like a copy-paste of every other 2000s YA fantasy. <br><br>We have Lia, who is exactly like every protagonist out there. She risks the peace between nations because she's worried that the prince might be ugly. And she ruins a perfectly good family heirloom while doing it. She's so predictable that I can guess every thing that comes out of her mouth, and I'm alarmingly good at it. <br><br>We have Pauline, Lia's maid, who throws away her perfectly comfortable life with a perfectly kind man to run away with some teenager who has no idea what she's doing. And then she has the nerve to say that this man "will know where she is no matter where she goes," because he "knows her like no other." Excuse me? <br><br>We have the Assassin (I lowkey forgot his name), who is also the worst killer in the entire history of killers. He's supposed to murder Lia, because she's risking the peace between kingdoms. But the moment he looks into her ~gorgeous eyes,~ he's lost to lurve. And suddenly he doesn't want to kill her, because <i>she's like no other girl he's ever met before...</i> *gags* <br><br>We have the Prince (haha, forgot his name too), who is just... he doesn't exist to me. He has absolutely no personality. I don't even know what to say about him because he's as shallow as a puddle. There's no character complexity here. <br><br><br><b>4. Good writing</b> <br><br>This was just alarmingly, painfully bad. Everything is told straight to my face. There's no depth. And the dialogue is horrible and cheesy and predictable. <br><br>I also found a number of plot holes. Lia and Pauline escape too easily, especially since two kingdoms are counting on them. They basically steal a horse and gallop away into the sunset. <br><br>And then they ride their horse through a stream to "conceal their tracks." *snorts* A horse is HEAVY. There is MUD at the bottom of a stream. And WATER PLANTS. Smashing water plants and stirring up mud and probably breaking your horse's leg by making it walk over stones is not going to help you at all. But Lia gets all happy because she's being so "clever." And Pauline's like "my lady, you are truly intelligent. So majestic." <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1602265553ra/30214589.gif" alt="Bang Head Against Wall GIFs | Tenor" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The descriptions were lazy, the pacing was so off, and their entire escape sequence was two pages long. It felt so hastily put-together, as if the editing team just fell asleep in the middle of reading this over. I don't blame them. I would be asleep, too. <br><br>DNF<br>1 star</span>
  <a data-text-id="15586464037342537031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HorA+8/Quyt/p9J1xt0fEKVBZLjPaSBcFmDOqNqv2ZUKo9JeYU6MwlZT1fYSZ4thqHbdM+BrrKe/v+QAWdHajQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aRnC66P/qgZh7j5KhrWP+ucaz1LDGsg9+YFHHgtbqrd9MNBODWGd70gaOclSDxuL6i122ewYRMZQXm22iCWprw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer13234020441066737072">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretendi</span>
  <span id="freeText13234020441066737072" style="display:none">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretending she was a spy with a bagful of amazing gadgets. She was rarely herself. Amazingly, she never broke a bone until she caught a basketball in gym class. Catching real balls was not her forte. These days she continues to live in make-believe worlds she creates in her books. Her latest 2-book series, <i>Dance of Thieves</i>, allows her do all kinds of dangerous things without breaking any bones. So far. <br />You can learn more about Mary and her books at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marypearson.com">www.marypearson.com</a><br /></span>

While she struggles to reach Morrighan and warn them, she finds herself at cross-purposes with Rafe and suspicious of Kaden, who has hunted her down.\n\nIn this conclusion to the Remnant Chronicles This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
